## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population P and time t, which is the fundamental problem in population dynamics. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent models like logistic and Gompertz equations.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, no density dependence)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population)
- Von Bertalanffy growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism vs catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible asymmetric growth)
- Beverton-Holt type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating birth rate minus death)
- Time-varying logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * t) (logistic with time-dependent parameters)
- Periodic carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (seasonal environment)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (generalized density-dependent growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * P) (exponentially declining per-capita rate)
- Time-delayed effect proxy: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 * t * P (time as proxy for delayed feedback)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence (negative feedback) → Terms with P multiplied by functions that decrease with P, e.g., P*(1 - c*P), P*log(c/P)
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → Cubic or product terms like P*(P - c1)*(c2 - P) creating growth rate that is negative at very low P
- Per-capita growth rate analysis → dP_dt/P should be examined; if linear in P → logistic; if log(P) → Gompertz
- Carrying capacity signature → dP_dt = 0 at a nonzero P value, implying factor (1 - c*P) or similar root-producing structure
- Metabolic scaling in populations → Fractional power laws P**c with c ≠ 1 reflecting allometric scaling of resource use
- Compensatory vs depensatory mortality → Ratio-dependent terms P/(c + P) indicate compensatory; P**2 terms indicate depensatory dynamics
- Environmental stochasticity proxy → Time-dependent multiplicative modulation of growth parameters, e.g., c0*(1 + c1*sin(c2*t))
- Conservation of mass/energy constraint → Growth terms balanced by loss terms of similar functional form but opposite sign

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (BPG4)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/(c4 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine if any candidate can match it.

**GT expression:**
$$0.1728(1 - P/48.55)P + \frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(-1.524(-0.924 + P))}$$

Let me expand this:
$$0.1728P - \frac{0.1728}{48.55}P^2 + \frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(-1.524P + 1.407)}$$

This simplifies to:
$$-0.003558P^2 + 0.1728P + \frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(1.407 - 1.524P)}$$

The sigmoid term can be rewritten: $\frac{0.1728P}{1 + \exp(1.407)\exp(-1.524P)}$

Note that $\exp(-1.524P) = \exp(-1.524P)$, so the third term involves $\frac{P}{1 + c\cdot e^{-aP}}$.

The GT has the form: $c_0 P^2 + c_1 P + \frac{c_2 P}{1 + c_3 \exp(-c_4 P)}$

This is a function of P only (no t dependence). Let me look for candidates that are functions of P only and can capture the sigmoid-like term $\frac{P}{1+\exp(\text{linear in }P)}$.

**Candidate 26:** $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + c_2 + c_3 \exp(c_4/(P+c_5))$
This has $\exp(c_4/(P+c_5))$, not a sigmoid form. Not equivalent.

**Candidate 31:** $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + \frac{P c_2}{P c_3 + c_4} + c_5 + \frac{c_6}{P c_3 + c_4}$
This gives rational functions, not sigmoid. Not equivalent.

**Candidate 35:** $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + \frac{P c_2}{P + c_3} + c_4 + \frac{c_5}{P c_6 + c_3}$
Rational functions only. Not equivalent.

The GT has a term $\frac{P}{1+\exp(\text{linear in }P)}$. I need candidates with exponential terms involving P in the right way.

**Candidate 27:** $P^2 c_0 + P c_1 + c_2 + c_3 \exp(c_4/P) + c_5 \log(c_6 \exp(Pc_7) + 1)$

Note: $\log(c_6 e^{c_7 P} + 1) = \log(e^{\ln c_6 + c_7 P} + 1)$. For large $c_7 P$, this approximates $\ln c_6 + c_7 P$. This is a softplus function, not a sigmoid times P. Not quite right.

Let me reconsider. The GT's sigmoid term: $\frac{0.1728P}{1+\exp(1.407-1.524P)}$. None of the candidates seem to have a $P/(1+\exp(\text{...}))$ structure.

**Candidate 2:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + c_2 + c_3\exp(c_4/(P+c_5)) + c_6/(Pc_7+1) + c_8/P$
The $\exp(c_4/(P+c_5))$ term cannot replicate $P/(1+\exp(\text{linear in }P))$.

**Candidate 3:** $P^2 c_0 + Pc_1 + Pc_2 + c_3 + c_4/(Pc_5+1) + c_6\exp(c_7/(P+c_8))$
Again $\exp(c_7/(P+c_8))$ is not sigmoid-like.

None of the candidates contain terms of the form $\exp(cP)$ in a denominator with P in the numerator, or equivalently a sigmoid function multiplied by P. The exponential terms in candidates are either $\exp(c/P)$, $\exp(c/(P+d))$, $\exp(cP)\cdot\log(...)$, or $\exp(ct)$ - none of which can produce $\frac{P}{1+\exp(\text{linear in }P)}$.

After thorough analysis, no candidate can reproduce the sigmoid-like term in the GT.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG4)
============================================================
GT: c0*(c1 - P/c2)*P + c3*P/(c4 + exp(-c5*(-c6 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.1728*(1 - P/48.55)*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(-0.924 + P)))`

Let me simplify the GT:
- First term: `0.1728*P - 0.003559*P²` (a linear + quadratic in P)
- Second term: `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*P + 1.408))` = `0.1728*P/(1 + exp(1.408)*exp(-1.524*P))`

So GT = `c_a*P² + c_b*P + 0.1728*P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(P - 0.924)))`

The key structural components are:
1. **P² term** (quadratic)
2. **P term** (linear)
3. **A sigmoidal term**: `P/(1 + exp(-c*(P - c')))` — this is P times a logistic sigmoid in P

This sigmoid term is crucial. Let me check which candidates can reproduce it.

The sigmoid `1/(1 + exp(-c*(P-c')))` cannot be represented by:
- Simple rational functions like `1/(P*c + 1)`
- `exp(c/P)` terms
- `log(P*c + 1)` terms
- Polynomial terms
- Terms involving `t`

Let me check candidates that might match:

**Candidates with `exp(c/(P+c))` structure:**
- Candidates 2, 3, 15, 19, 23, 26, 29, 39, 43, 44, 47

The GT sigmoid is `1/(1 + exp(-c5*(P - c6)))`. Can `exp(c/(P+c'))` match `1/(1+exp(-c*(P-c')))`? No — `exp(c/(P+c'))` is fundamentally different from `1/(1+exp(linear in P))`. The sigmoid has a specific S-shaped transition that `exp(c/P)` cannot replicate exactly.

**Candidates with `exp(c*P)` or similar:**
- Candidate 27: has `c5*log(c6*exp(P*c7) + 1)` — this is a softplus! `log(c6*exp(c7*P) + 1)` = `log(c6) + log(exp(c7*P) + 1/c6)`. This doesn't directly give `P/(1+exp(...))`.

**Candidates with `P/(P*c + 1)` rational terms:**
These give `P/(cP+1)` which approaches a constant for large P, unlike the sigmoid*P which approaches P for large P.

**Candidates with `t` dependence:**
GT has no `t` dependence. Candidates with `t` terms can only match if all `t`-dependent coefficients can be set to 0. Let me check those.

Going through systematically, the GT's sigmoid term `P/(1 + exp(-1.524*(P-0.924)))` is a very specific nonlinear function. None of the candidate basis functions — rational functions, `exp(c/P)`, `log(cP+1)`, `exp(cP)*log(...)`, power terms `P^c` — can exactly reproduce a logistic sigmoid in P.

The only way to get a logistic sigmoid is through `1/(1 + exp(linear in P))`, and none of the candidates contain this structure.

Let me verify: No candidate has `1/(1 + exp(c*P))` or equivalent sigmoid structure. The `exp(c/(P+c'))` terms in several candidates produce a fundamentally different function shape.

After careful analysis, **none of the candidates** can exactly reproduce the sigmoidal component of the GT.
